Une fois que les joueurs commencent à dessiner des tuiles, ils sont généralement placés sur le bord avant les joueurs, de sorte que chaque joueur peut voir ses propres dominos, mais aucun ne peut voir la valeur des tuiles des autres joueurs. Dans différents jeux, les premières tuiles sont également différentes. Cette tuile commence la ligne de jeu, une série de tuiles dans lesquelles des tuiles adjacentes touchent avec des valeurs correspondantes, c'est-à-dire égales. Les joueurs étendent alternativement la ligne de jeu avec une tuile à l'une de ses deux extrémités. Le jeu se termine lorsqu'un joueur gagne en jouant sa dernière tuile, ou lorsque la partie est bloquée parce qu'aucun joueur ne peut jouer. Si cela se produit, la personne qui a provoqué le blocage obtient tous les points de joueur restants sans compter les siens.\r\n- Jeu de notation\r\nLes joueurs accumulent des points pendant le jeu pour certaines configurations, se déplace ou vident la main. Only the tiles adjacent to the empty space can be moved (either horizontally or vertically).\r\nFloTiles builds upon this simple concept. In FloTiles too, the image (or a number series) is split into several smaller tiles to form a GameBoard of m x n rows which are then jumbled. The similarity with a jigsaw puzzle stops here. No tiles are removed so there is no empty space to move adjacent tiles. Instead, the user can drag a tile from any location in the GameBoard and place it in any other location. The other tiles also readjust automatically to accommodate the tile in its new position. Now it may look like the player now has a lot of freedom and the game has become easier. The truth is, it is not. :)\r\nThe USP of FloTiles lies in the way the user has to arrange the tiles to obtain the final image. This arrangement of the tiles is termed as FloPattern .\r\n\r\nWorkflow\r\nEach of the FloPattern represents a challenge. Each challenge contains 9 levels representing a GameBoard of a particular size. In these levels :\r\n(i) The first level will be a trial level of size 5x5 . Also the tiles will not contain sections of the images. Instead they will contain numbers from 1 to 25. The user can play this level to get a feel of how the FloPattern behaves whenever the user moves a tile. This will also help the user to build a strategy to solve the puzzle in later levels. However it is optional for the user to play this level.\r\n(ii) The next 8 levels will be having GameBoard sizes ranging from 3x3 to 10x10 .\r\nInitially, all the levels and levels (except the practice level and the first level in the Straight Shot Challenge - I) will be locked. Successful completion of a level will unlock the next level in the challenge.\r\n\r\nSuccessful completion of the first five levels of any challenge will unlock the next challenge. The last three levels (of sizes 8x8, 9x9 and 10x10) are of high complexity and may require considerable time and patience from the user. Thus they are optional for the user to complete and they can be skipped to proceed to the next challenge. However the user is free to complete the last three levels first before proceeding to the next challenge.\r\n\r\nDuring the game, the user is presented with 4 options in the Bottom AppBar which can be accessed by swiping from the bottom of the screen upwards. Classic is a fast and frenzied card game has been a family favorite for over four decades now. Featuring a balanced mix of gentle strategy and chance, it’s entertaining for all ages and can be played anywhere.\r\n\r\nIt is a pretty popular game, and for a good reason: it's a game that's very simple to learn, but still has some strategic complexity. It's on the shallow end of complexity. \r\n\r\nThe objective of the game is to get rid of your cards fast to win this game! \r\n\r\nBut Uno Classic game not just a feast of fun – it also helps develop kids counting, matching, critical thinking, and social interaction.\r\n\r\nUno is a simple color and number matching game. The deck consists of 108 cards, of which there are 25 of each color (red, green, blue, and yellow), each color having two of each rank except zero. The ranks in each color are zero to nine, \"Skip\", \"Draw Two\", and \"Reverse\" (the last three being \"action cards\"). In addition, the deck contains four each of \"Wild\" and \"Wild Draw Four\" cards\r\n\r\nEach player is dealt 7 cards and the remaining cards are placed face down to form a draw pile. \r\nThe first player has to match the card in the discard pile either by number or color or the player can throw down a Wild Card else he must pick a card from the draw pile. If he can play what is drawn, great. The game and its variants are popular in many countries and under various names.\r\n\r\nParchisi originated in India by the 6th century. \r\n\r\nEach player rolls the die; the highest roller begins the game. Players alternate turns in a clockwise direction.\r\n\r\nLudo can be played by two, three, or four, without partnerships. To enter a token into play from its yard to its starting square, a player must roll a 6. If the player has no tokens yet in play and rolls other than a 6, the turn passes to the next player. Once a player has one or more tokens in play, he selects a token and moves it forwards along the track the number of squares indicated by the dice. Players must always move a token according to the die value rolled. Passes are not allowed; if no move is possible, the turn moves to the next player.\r\n\r\nPlayers may not end their move on a square they already occupy. If the advance of a token ends on a square occupied by an opponent's token, the opponent token is returned to its owner's yard. The returned token can be reentered into play only when the owner rolls a 6. \r\n\r\nThe first person to move all 4 pieces into the home wins.\r\n\r\nHave you ever missed the classic family
